Two listeners, on user specified ports or\\n147: \\t// unix domain sockets could have completely different sets of\\n148: \\t// services. So a global list of services per sidecar scope will be\\n149: \\t// incorrect. Hence the per listener set of services.\\n150: \\tservices []*Service\\n151: \\n152: \\t// List of virtual services imported by this egress listener above.\\n153: \\t// As with per listener services, this\\n154: \\t// will be used by RDS code to compute the virtual host configs for\\n155: \\t// http listeners, as well as by TCP/TLS filter code to compute the\\n156: \\t// service routing configs and the filter chain matches. We need a\\n157: \\t// virtualService set per listener and not one per sidecarScope because\\n158: \\t// each listener imports an independent set of virtual services.\\n159: \\t// Listener 1 could import a public virtual service for serviceA from\\n160: \\t// namespace A that has some path rewrite, while listener2 could import\\n161: \\t// a private virtual service for serviceA from the local namespace,\\n162: \\t// with a different path rewrite or no path rewrites.\\n163: \\tvirtualServices []config.Config\\n164: \\n165: \\tlistenerHosts map[string][]host.Name\\n166: }\\n167: \\n168: const defaultSidecar = \\\"default-sidecar\\\"\\n169: \\n170: // DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace is a sidecar scope object with a default catch all egress listener\\n171: // that matches the default Istio behavior: a sidecar has listeners for all services in the mesh\\n172: // We use this scope when the user has not set any sidecar Config for a given config namespace.\\n173: func DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace(ps *PushContext, configNamespace string) *SidecarScope {\\n174: \\tdefaultEgressListener := &IstioEgressListenerWrapper{\\n175: \\t\\tIstioListener: is a wrapper over the Sidecar resource with some\n56: // preprocessed data to determine the list of services, virtualServices,\n57: // and destinationRules that are accessible to a given\n58: // sidecar. Precomputing the list of services, virtual services, dest rules\n59: // for a sidecar improves performance as we no longer need to compute this\n60: // list for every sidecar. We simply have to match a sidecar to a\n61: // SidecarScope. Note that this is not the same as public/private scoped\n62: // services. The list of services seen by every sidecar scope (namespace\n63: // wide or per workload) depends on the imports, the listeners, and other\n64: // settings.\n65: //\n66: // Every proxy workload of SidecarProxy type will always map to a\n67: // SidecarScope object. If the proxy's namespace does not have a user\n68: // specified Sidecar CRD, we will construct one that has a catch all egress\n69: // listener that imports every public service/virtualService in the mesh.\n70: type SidecarScope struct {\n71: \tName string\n72: \t// This is the namespace where the sidecar takes effect,\n73: \t// maybe different from the ns where sidecar resides if sidecar is in root ns.\n74: \tNamespace string\n75: \t// The crd itself. Each hostname in this map\n98: \t// corresponds to a service in the services array above. for example each K8S cluster is a registry\\n260: // instance. Each registry is responsible for tracking a set\\n261: // of endpoints associated with mesh services, and calling the EDSUpdate on changes.\\n262: // A registry may group endpoints for a service in smaller subsets - for example by\\n263: // deployment, or to deal with very large number of endpoints for a service. We want\\n264: // to avoid passing around large objects - like full list of endpoints for a registry,\\n265: // or the full list of endpoints for a service across registries, since it limits\\n266: // scalability.\\n267: //\\n268: // Future optimizations will include grouping the endpoints by labels, gateway or region to\\n269: // reduce the time when subsetting or split-horizon is used. This design assumes pilot\\n270: // tracks all endpoints in the mesh and they fit in RAM - so limit is few M endpoints.\\n271: // It is possible to split the endpoint tracking in future.\\n272: type XDSUpdater interface {\\n273: \\t// EDSUpdate is called when the list of endpoints or labels in a Service is changed.\\n274: \\t// For each cluster and hostname, the full list of active endpoints (including empty list)\\n275: \\t// must be sent. The shard name is used as a key - current implementation is using the\\n276: \\t// registry name.\\n277: \\tEDSUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, entry []*IstioEndpoint)\\n278: \\n279: \\t// EDSCacheUpdate is called when the list of endpoints or labels in a Service is changed.\\n280: \\t// For each cluster and hostname, the full list of active endpoints (including empty list)\\n281: \\t// must be sent. The shard name is used as a key - current implementation is using the\\n282: \\t// registry name.\\n283: \\t// Note: the difference with `EDSUpdate` is that it only update the cache rather than requesting a push\\n284: \\tEDSCacheUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, entry []*IstioEndpoint)\\n285: \\n286: \\t// SvcUpdate is called when a service definition is updated/deleted.\\n287: \\tSvcUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, event Event)\\n288: \\n289: \\t// ConfigUpdate is called to notify the XDS server of config updates and request a push.\\n290: \\t// The requests may be collapsed and throttled.\\n291: \\tConfigUpdate(req *PushRequest)\\n292: \\n293: \\t// ProxyUpdate is called to notify the XDS server to send a push to the specified proxy.\\n294: \\t// The requests may be collapsed and throttled.\\n295: \\tProxyUpdate(clusterID cluster.ID, ip string)\\n296: \\n297: \\t// RemoveShard removes all endpoints for the given shard key\\n298: \\tRemoveShard(shardKey ShardKey)\\n299: }\\n300: \\n301: {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Ji6B5Jm3ih8XYeN9F8zv1R","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_017bYqgjNKyiNbSkSY7rb5dW","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report\n\n## Summary\n\nWhen multiple DestinationRules target the same host, Istio merges them into a single consolidated configuration. However, only the first DestinationRule's metadata (name/namespace) is retained in the merged structure, causing all other contributing DRs to lose their identity. Later, when SidecarScope registers config dependencies for xDS push filtering, it only registers the surviving DR's metadata. This causes updates to non-surviving DRs to be invisible to the push filter, resulting in stale Envoy configuration.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**The root cause is a two-part failure in metadata preservation during DestinationRule merging:**\n\n1. **Metadata loss during merging** (`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`): The `mergeDestinationRule()` function consolidates multiple DRs for the same host into a single `config.Config` object in the `consolidatedDestRules` structure. When a second DR is merged into an existing one, only the first DR's `config.Meta` (Name/Namespace) is preserved. The second DR's metadata is discarded.\n\n2. **Incomplete dependency registration** (`pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:219-227, 410-416`): When SidecarScope builds its config dependencies, it iterates over the merged destination rules. Since the merged structure only contains one `config.Config` per hostname (due to step 1), only that one DR's ConfigKey (Kind, Name, Namespace) gets registered in `configDependencies`.\n\n3. **Push filter bypass** (`pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go:60-74`): When a config update event occurs, the xDS push filter calls `SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig()` to check if the proxy depends on the updated config. The check uses a hash computed from the ConfigKey's Name, Namespace, and Kind. If the updated DR was the one whose metadata was lost during merging, its hash won't exist in `configDependencies`, causing `DependsOnConfig()` to return false and the push to be incorrectly skipped.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### File: `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go`\n\n**Function: `mergeDestinationRule()` (lines 38-109)**\n- Line 41: `if mdrList, exists := p.destRules[resolvedHost]; exists {`\n- Line 66: `p.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied` — Updates the existing DR in-place with merged content\n- Lines 77-87: Subsets from new DR are appended to existing DR's subsets\n- Lines 91-92: Traffic policy from new DR is merged into existing DR if not present\n- **Missing**: No code to preserve the second DR's metadata; it's discarded after merging\n\n### File: `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`\n\n**Function: `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` (lines 219-227)**\n```go\nfor _, drList := range out.destinationRules {\n    for _, dr := range drList {\n        out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n            Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n            Name:      dr.Name,              // Only the surviving DR's name\n            Namespace: dr.Namespace,          // Only the surviving DR's namespace\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Function: `ConvertToSidecarScope()` (lines 410-416)**\n```go\nfor _, dr := range drList {\n    out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n        Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n        Name:      dr.Name,                  // Only the surviving DR's name\n        Namespace: dr.Namespace,              // Only the surviving DR's namespace\n    })\n}\n```\n\nBoth functions only register dependencies for DRs that appear in the final merged list.\n\n### File: `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`\n\n**Function: `DependsOnConfig()` (lines 523-540)**\n```go\nfunc (sc *SidecarScope) DependsOnConfig(config ConfigKey) bool {\n    if sc == nil {\n        return true\n    }\n\n    if _, f := clusterScopedConfigTypes[config.Kind]; f {\n        return config.Namespace == sc.RootNamespace || config.Namespace == sc.Namespace\n    }\n\n    if _, f := sidecarScopeKnownConfigTypes[config.Kind]; !f {\n        return true\n    }\n\n    _, exists := sc.configDependencies[config.HashCode()]  // Line 538: Lookup in dependencies\n    return exists                                            // Line 539: Returns false if not found\n}\n```\n\nIf the ConfigKey for an updated DR is not in `configDependencies` (because it was merged and lost its identity), this function returns false.\n\n### File: `pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go`\n\n**Function: `checkProxyDependencies()` (lines 60-74)**\n```go\nfunc checkProxyDependencies(proxy *model.Proxy, config model.ConfigKey) bool {\n    switch proxy.Type {\n    case model.SidecarProxy:\n        if proxy.SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(config) {\n            return true\n        } else if proxy.PrevSidecarScope != nil && proxy.PrevSidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(config) {\n            return true\n        }\n    default:\n        return true\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\n\nThis calls `DependsOnConfig()` which returns false for merged-away DRs, causing the entire `ConfigAffectsProxy()` check to fail.\n\n**Function: `ConfigAffectsProxy()` (lines 32-58)**\n```go\nfunc ConfigAffectsProxy(req *model.PushRequest, proxy *model.Proxy) bool {\n    if len(req.ConfigsUpdated) == 0 {\n        return true\n    }\n\n    for config := range req.ConfigsUpdated {\n        affected := true\n\n        if kindAffectedTypes, f := configKindAffectedProxyTypes[config.Kind]; f {\n            affected = false\n            for _, t := range kindAffectedTypes {\n                if t == proxy.Type {\n                    affected = true\n                    break\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        if affected && checkProxyDependencies(proxy, config) {  // Line 52: Calls checkProxyDependencies\n            return true\n        }\n    }\n\n    return false\n}\n```\n\nIf `checkProxyDependencies()` returns false, the proxy won't be pushed.\n\n### File: `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`\n\n**Function: `SetDestinationRules()` (lines 1672-1768)**\n- Lines 1716 and 1739: Calls `ps.mergeDestinationRule()` for each DR\n- This populates the `destinationRuleIndex` with only the surviving merged DRs\n- Example (lines 1764-1766):\n```go\nps.destinationRuleIndex.namespaceLocal = namespaceLocalDestRules      // Contains merged DRs only\nps.destinationRuleIndex.exportedByNamespace = exportedDestRulesByNamespace\nps.destinationRuleIndex.rootNamespaceLocal = rootNamespaceLocalDestRules\n```\n\n**Function: `destinationRule()` (lines 990-1066)**\n- This function retrieves merged destination rules from the index\n- Returns `[]*config.Config` but the list only contains the surviving merged DRs\n- No way to trace back to the original contributing DRs\n\n### File: `pilot/pkg/model/config.go`\n\n**Type: `ConfigKey` (lines 54-58)**\n```go\ntype ConfigKey struct {\n    Kind      config.GroupVersionKind\n    Name      string\n    Namespace string\n}\n```\n\n**Function: `HashCode()` (lines 60-74)**\n```go\nfunc (key ConfigKey) HashCode() uint64 {\n    hash := md5.New()\n    for _, v := range []string{\n        key.Name,\n        key.Namespace,\n        key.Kind.Kind,\n        key.Kind.Group,\n        key.Kind.Version,\n    } {\n        hash.Write([]byte(v))\n    }\n    // ...\n    return binary.BigEndian.Uint64(sum)\n}\n```\n\nThe hash is computed from Name and Namespace. If these are not registered in `configDependencies`, the hash won't match during xDS push filtering.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go`** — DestinationRule merging not just the consolidated one\n- This maintains full traceability and ensures any update to any contributing DR triggers a push\n\n**Option 2: Create a synthetic \"consolidated\" DR ConfigKey**\n- synthetic key in configDependencies\n- This is complex because it requires intercepting config update events\n\n**Option 3: Re-index on every update**\n- Instead of caching merged DRs, re-compute However, only the first DestinationRule's metadata (name/namespace) is retained in the merged structure, causing all other contributing DRs to lose their identity. Later, when SidecarScope registers config dependencies for xDS push filtering, it only registers the surviving DR's metadata. This causes updates to non-surviving DRs to be invisible to the push filter, resulting in stale Envoy configuration.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**The root cause is a two-part failure in metadata preservation during DestinationRule merging:**\n\n1. **Metadata loss during merging** (`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`): The `mergeDestinationRule()` function consolidates multiple DRs for the same host into a single `config.Config` object in the `consolidatedDestRules` structure. When a second DR is merged into an existing one, only the first DR's `config.Meta` (Name/Namespace) is preserved. The second DR's metadata is discarded.\n\n2. **Incomplete dependency registration** (`pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:219-227, 410-416`): When SidecarScope builds its config dependencies, it iterates over the merged destination rules. Since the merged structure only contains one `config.Config` per hostname (due to step 1), only that one DR's ConfigKey (Kind, Name, Namespace) gets registered in `configDependencies`.\n\n3. **Push filter bypass** (`pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go:60-74`): When a config update event occurs, the xDS push filter calls `SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig()` to check if the proxy depends on the updated config. The check uses a hash computed from the ConfigKey's Name, Namespace, and Kind. If the updated DR was the one whose metadata was lost during merging, its hash won't exist in `configDependencies`, causing `DependsOnConfig()` to return false and the push to be incorrectly skipped.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### File: `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go`\n\n**Function: `mergeDestinationRule()` (lines 38-109)**\n- Line 41: `if mdrList, exists := p.destRules[resolvedHost]; it's discarded after merging\n\n### File: `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`\n\n**Function: `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` (lines 219-227)**\n```go\nfor _, drList := range out.destinationRules {\n    for _, dr := range drList {\n        out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n            Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n            Name:      dr.Name,              // Only the surviving DR's name\n            Namespace: dr.Namespace,          // Only the surviving DR's namespace\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Function: `ConvertToSidecarScope()` (lines 410-416)**\n```go\nfor _, dr := range drList {\n    out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n        Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n        Name:      dr.Name,                  // Only the surviving DR's name\n        Namespace: dr.Namespace,              // Only the surviving DR's namespace\n    })\n}\n```\n\nBoth functions only register dependencies for DRs that appear in the final merged list.\n\n### File: `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`\n\n**Function: `DependsOnConfig()` (lines 523-540)**\n```go\nfunc (sc *SidecarScope) DependsOnConfig(config ConfigKey) bool {\n    if sc == nil {\n        return true\n    }\n\n    if _, f := clusterScopedConfigTypes[config.Kind]; However, only the first DestinationRule's metadata (name/namespace) is retained in the merged structure, causing all other contributing DRs to lose their identity. Later, when SidecarScope registers config dependencies for xDS push filtering, it only registers the surviving DR's metadata. This causes updates to non-surviving DRs to be invisible to the push filter, resulting in stale Envoy configuration.\n     6→\n     7→## Root Cause\n     8→\n     9→**The root cause is a two-part failure in metadata preservation during DestinationRule merging:**\n    10→\n    11→1. **Metadata loss during merging** (`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`): The `mergeDestinationRule()` function consolidates multiple DRs for the same host into a single `config.Config` object in the `consolidatedDestRules` structure. When a second DR is merged into an existing one, only the first DR's `config.Meta` (Name/Namespace) is preserved. The second DR's metadata is discarded.\n    12→\n    13→2. **Incomplete dependency registration** (`pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:219-227, 410-416`): When SidecarScope builds its config dependencies, it iterates over the merged destination rules. Since the merged structure only contains one `config.Config` per hostname (due to step 1), only that one DR's ConfigKey (Kind, Name, Namespace) gets registered in `configDependencies`.\n    14→\n    15→3. **Push filter bypass** (`pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go:60-74`): When a config update event occurs, the xDS push filter calls `SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig()` to check if the proxy depends on the updated config. The check uses a hash computed from the ConfigKey's Name, Namespace, and Kind. If the updated DR was the one whose metadata was lost during merging, its hash won't exist in `configDependencies`, causing `DependsOnConfig()` to return false and the push to be incorrectly skipped.\n    16→\n    17→## Evidence\n    18→\n    19→### File: `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go`\n    20→\n    21→**Function: `mergeDestinationRule()` (lines 38-109)**\n    22→- Line 41: `if mdrList, exists := p.destRules[resolvedHost]; exists {`\n    23→- Line 66: `p.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied` — Updates the existing DR in-place with merged content\n    24→- Lines 77-87: Subsets from new DR are appended to existing DR's subsets\n    25→- Lines 91-92: Traffic policy from new DR is merged into existing DR if not present\n    26→- **Missing**: No code to preserve the second DR's metadata; it's discarded after merging\n    27→\n    28→### File: `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`\n    29→\n    30→**Function: `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` (lines 219-227)**\n    31→```go\n    32→for _, drList := range out.destinationRules {\n    33→    for _, dr := range drList {\n    34→        out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n    35→            Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n    36→            Name:      dr.Name,              // Only the surviving DR's name\n    37→            Namespace: dr.Namespace,          // Only the surviving DR's namespace\n    38→        })\n    39→    }\n    40→}\n    41→```\n    42→\n    43→**Function: `ConvertToSidecarScope()` (lines 410-416)**\n    44→```go\n    45→for _, dr := range drList {\n    46→    out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n    47→        Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n    48→        Name:      dr.Name,                  // Only the surviving DR's name\n    49→        Namespace: dr.Namespace,              // Only the surviving DR's namespace\n    50→    })\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
